text:
This is a great recipe!  Thanks for sharing.  I did make a few additions as others did.  The great thing about this recipe is you can tailor it to your tastes without any problem.  I used a whole onion.  I added celery, shredded carrots as well as basil, oregano, marjoram, cayenne pepper and a few red pepper flakes.  As a final touch I added some thinly sliced smoked sauasge.  And as always, when I make any soup I use boxed chicken stock.  It is so much more flavorful than boullion or broth and not nearly as salty.  After simmering together for less than an hour it tasted like it had cooked all day.  So flavorful and wonderful!!! Will definitely make again.

text:
I made this soup for its healing benefits, but I ended up loving it so much I'd make it anytime! It truly is "healing" and not just for cold/flu season, but this could also greatly benefit those with certain digestive conditions. (Cabbage being excellent for stomach ulcers, for one thing.) I found the amount of cabbage in the original recipe to be just right and did not add extra as other reviewers did. I did however, increase the onion to a whole medium-sized onion instead of just half, and used 4 garlic cloves instead of 2. I also added a little Italian seasoning to it, a pinch of cayenne, and a little black pepper.

text:
9/2013 I've made this many times and love it. Whenever I can, I add some kind of protein... usually beans (pinto, garbanzo, black...doesn't matter). The other option is serving over some leftover  shredded chicken. It may just be soup, but with a little thought the nutritional value is excellent.

I found this recipe to be perfect as written. It is not supposed to be a thick soup, but a consume based one. I think there is confusion about how much cabbage to add because they do vary in size alot.  Maybe trying to pin down a weight (like 1/2 of a 2 lb head) would give a little more guidance. Thanks for a great recipe!

text:
I decided to try this last night since I'm fighting a cold.  It was delicious!  I did make a few changes though, which is why I only gave it four stars.  

I used 8 chicken bouillon cubes instead of 4, plus I added extra herbs & a pinch of red pepper flakes as someone suggested.  I substituted 1/2 tsp. onion powder for the onion and used more garlic than called for.  Since I left out the onion, I only needed 1 tsp. of olive oil to sautee the garlic.  

We served the soup with some French bread brushed with olive oil and sprinkled with garlic salt & Parmesan cheese then toasted.  It was an excellent meal!

Even though I'm not big on soup, I enjoyed my first bowl of it tonight.  I used half chicken broth & half water, because I don't like strong broth.  Also used a whole onion & whole cabbage, & plain stewed tomatoes; added Italian seasoning & omitted salt.  If I do it again I would use fresh plum tomatoes in place of canned, because I prefer to stay with whole foods & avoid added sugar, salt, high fructose corn syrup, etc.  This is definitely a nice way to use cabbage.  Will probably do this one again.  I gave it a 4 because of the use of convenience ingredients which are not healthy.

text:
Several days after coming home from surgery, I sent my husband to the grocery store with lettuce on the list. Well the angels were watching over him & he came home with cabbage instead. I found this recipe which contained ingredients I had, or had reasonable substitutes. And with a name like that how could I resist? My "I'm not a cook" husband chopped all the veggies and it was easy enough for me to put it all together. We just finished it and it was great. So comforting. Real food. I feel better already.
I used 2 tablespoons olive oil which was enough. With the onion (used a whole small one) and garlic, I also cooked some celery and green pepper. I used "better than bouillon chicken base" which I use in place of bouillon in all my soups. 1/2 teaspoon pepper was just right for us but 1/2 teaspoon salt was plenty. I thought I'd want more than 1/2 of the large cabbage I had--but 1/2 was fine. I used diced tomatoes with balsamic vinegar, basil & olive oil.  It turned out great.

text:
I just made this recipe tonight.  It is probably one of my top 10.... the best/easiest thing you could ever wish for!!  Instead of bouillon cubes and the two quarts of water, I used only two cans of reduced sodium chicken broth, because after making this recipe a few times, I realized that I prefer it have much less liquid.  I did not add salt, and added 1/2 tsp of crushed red pepper flakes as well for a kick.  The thing about having less liquid in this soup is that it can be served as soup, or other times you may prefer to drain away some of the liquid and actually serve it as a tasty side to any simple pork chop or chicken dish.  I make this at least once a month and it's enough for 8 servings for us, even with the reduced liquid.  At times, I use only ONE can of chicken broth when I know that I plan on serving this as a side dish and not a soup.  It's still every bit as delicious!

text:
I did make a number of changes, although I suspect that the soup would be wonderufl as posted.  I list my modifications so that others may benefit from my experience; as others have said, this recipe is perfect for local tailoring!

I began by browning chunks of lean pork (I used cubed boneless country-style "ribs") in olive oil with the garlic and onion .... and generous sprinkling of herbs de provence.  Once the pork cubes were brown, I added three bags of slaw mix, one large can of chicken broth, and three cans of diced Italian-style tomatoes.  This I simmered for about 45 mins.  Then, with the heat OFF, I stirred in about two cups of frozen peas (which were able to cook in the residual heat).   Oh ... I also added a genrous sprinkle of fresh-ground pepper.  Yum.  Relatively low-fat and relatively low-sodium!  Today was the second day I carried it to my office for lunch.  Don't think I'll be tired of it by Friday!

Sorry to be so long-winded ... and to have deviated so much from the original recipe, but I wanted to share my delight in my new soup discovery!

This recipe came at a perfect time.  I needed to use up a pkg of slaw mix and the date was going to expire.  The only changes I made (and you could do a lot of personalizing on this one)were to add celery, a little more onion and diced carrot and subst one can of chicken broth for part of the water in addition to the granules. And I used the entire can of tomatoes and pureed them before adding them to the soup. Also added a scoop of cooked rice to each seving.  This is great if you are sick or well and it would be very soothing if you are sick with cold/flu.  Thanks, JG from Susie

text:
Really delicious soup! I added corn to the soup to give it a little more bulk. Also, to make it a little thicker, I took about half of the soup, put it in the blender, pureed it, and added it back to the stock pot. This really helped with the texture. I also let it simmer, uncovered, for about 2 hours to thicken it up as well. Overall, it was very tasty and cheap to make too, which was great for a starving college student.

I'm a cabbage fanatic and made hubby meatloaf for dinner and I don't like so decided to whip up something that would be nice and warm...this fit the bill.  I had the Italian diced tomatoes and also added 1 roma tomato that was starting to look kind of sad.  I used Swanson chicken broth w/roasted garlic (it's really good canned broth) and then some chicken bouillon/water.  I had some baby carrots I had made and couldn't choke down on their own (balsamic carrots) so threw those in, and I had one lonely turnip down in the crisper so diced that up and threw in.  Put this on the stove while I whipped up a batch of cookies and was done by the time the first batch came out of the oven....I did have to add a little more salt to mine but that's personal preference.  Also added a bit of harissa chile powder for some 'heat'.  This could easily be embellished with the 'clean out the fridge' bunch of veggies.  lo to no fat and very, very healthy.

text:
I received this as a daily email from Allrecipe. I looked at it, read all the reviews and thought I like cabbage but in a soup?..Today I wanted something to make to go along with my Sunday meal making for week ahead.  Worked with what I had on hand. I used a bag of frozen seasoning vegetables (onions, celery,red and green peppers)thawed.  Minced garlic.  Do not use bouillion, so used 4 cans of chicken broth. Omitted the salt.  Added 2 carrot sliced thin. Didn't have a head of cabbage but I did have a bag of cole slaw mix. No Italian style stewed tomatoes but did have diced. Sauted the veggies,and garlic, added the black pepper, and thyme,which I put in all my soups, crushed caraway seed,because it goes good with cabbage and dash of italian spices to make up for stewed tomatoes.  Added the cole slaw.. then the tomatoes undrained.  And let it go. I ended up eating two bowls of soup and the Sunday dinner is now leftovers for during week.  This was delicious and using the short cuts made it even better and I am sure it didn't compromise the taste. Thanks for a great base..will be making this often.

text:
A healthy, hearty, filling and cheap soup.  Just what I was looking for.  The directions couldn't be easier, nor could the ingredients be more simple-- all that and it even tastes good.  I made a double batch and had it for lunch at work every day this week, and I'm still not tired of it.

The reviewer who suggested Parmesan cheese was right on.  When I first made the soup, I served it for dinner with a crusty French baguette that I cut into slices, basted with olive oil and garlic powder, sprinkled with a Parmesan/Romano mix and then toasted under the broiler.  I also garnished my soup with some of the cheese mixture, which was great.  

I made my soup pretty spicy by adding some Cayenne and a good amount of fresh ground black pepper.  My nose runs every time I eat it, so I'm sure this would be perfect for healing a cold.  I ate it in perfect health and on the hottest day of the year, though!  I think it's tasty anytime.

I just made this and my husband and I thought it was very good and will make it again. That being said, I looked at this recipe first because I wanted cabbage soup. I read many reviews and barely any are for the recipe. The reviews are based on using it as a base and putting in whatever you want, and still calling it this recipe. If you add a bunch of vegetables, it becomes vegetable soup. there are recipes for vegetable soup. If you put meat in it, it is no longer cabbage soup, but something else, that there  are recipes for. Obviously, everyone who changed it, wasn't really looking for cabbage soup. We all do our own thing with cooking, but I get tired of reading reviews that just change the recipes. And since they change everything, the amount of reviews becomes deceitful and misleading.

This is sooo delicious and hearty!! It really hit the spot this cold winter night! I doubled the recipe and used red cabbage because that was what I had and I followed the recipe, for the most part, but I didn't follow it strictly because this recipe is great for personalizing. Also, I threw in the tomatoes as is without draining them---I like the extra tomatoe flavor and nutrients!

text:
This is one of the easiest soups to make and it's one of my favorites. It's very tangy and fresh tasting. The veggies are not mushy as long as you don't overcook. I stop cooking when they are still nice and firm with just a little "bite" to them. I think you have to like Bloody Marys, tomato juice or V8 to enjoy this soup because it does have a lot of zing from the tomatoes and other veggies, but if you are a huge fan like me you will love it. As with any recipe here, only add salt to taste. I never trust another person's salt threshold.

I just made this soup tonight after a long day of Christmas cookie baking.  It was quick to throw together.  Took advice of others and used chix. broth, water and 1 chix. bouillon cube instead of all chix bouillon.  Added chopped celery to onions, cooked till tender.  I bought the wrong size tomatoes, got a very large can, twice the size called for, but added it all anyway.  Added some sliced smoked polish sausage, carrots, and about 2 Tbls. sugar to take the bite out of the tomatoes.  It tasted great on a cold winter nite here in Wisconsin.  I bet it will taste even better tomorrow after flavors have time to mingle.

text:
Once you make a few minor adjustments this soup will become a staple. I highly recommend, as others suggested, using chicken broth and no water. I used some leftover broth I had and five cups water so to give it a broth flavor I ended up adding in 4 tbsp. of chicken bouillon.  Adding in a pinch of cayenne pepper also gives it a boost of flavor. When adding in the onion I also included red potatoes, frozen corn, green bell pepper, and fresh parsley and crumbled up some fried bacon once it came to the step of adding in the canned tomatoes. Bake some sweet cornbread alongside in the oven and it's sure to please. Hope this helps ya‚Äôll, enjoy and happy stewing!

text:
Better than chicken soup! So simple, so tasty and so easy to make. This recipe is fantastic as is, without any alterations.

That said, the small changes we like to make are upping the pepper a bit; throwing an egg in the next-day leftovers to give the soup a bit more protein and heft; add cooked rice. Adding the juices from the canned Italian spice tomatoes gives the soup a great taste, too. 

And by the way, it does not freeze well. We found that out the hard way! Regardless, this is our go-to soup in the winter whenever one of us is feeling the chill or just a little under the weather.

This is a great basic soup that's easy to make your own. I don't like chopping vegetables, so when I was in Trader Joe's I purchased pre-chopped mirepoix for this batch, definitely worth the $2.99. In the past I've used the frozen chopped onion and it works well, but the addition of carrot and celery in the mirepoix was great in this soup. I also added some turmeric since it is anti-inflammatory and gives the soup a deeper color. In the past I've added a good quality Hungarian paprika to the onion and oil in the beginning, which is also very good. I decided to try this batch in the Instant Pot for a change. I plan on making this all winter!

text:
I'm a serious "soup-guy" and made a number of my own.  But this is definitely one of my all-time favorites! I have made it many times and have never been disappointed. Loved it the first time done as directed, and it immediately became a solid "soup staple" for my family as it is easy and delicious and gets better over time. I have probably made it 6 times. As there are 3 of us in the household and always with different hours and always "on the go", to come home and have to put together a meal when tired can be a drag. But a hot bowl of soup retrieved from a pot in the 'fridge' is just the ticket.
It's adaptability is amazing. I now always use some meat, (diced or shredded chicken),(also large sliced mild-spicy sausages). An extra veg is nice, too. A note: If it is meant to last 2-3 days, best to be easy on the cabbage at the initial cooking as it is delicate and sitting for a time in the 'fridge' can become a bit soggy. Better to boil an add fresh to the later bowls.
Delicious, and ridiculously healthy, I highly recommend this to anyone.

text:
My husband just happens to be down with a cold this morning and I was looking for a soup recipe that wasn't the standard chicken noodle, since he's not too keen on chicken. I'm so glad I found this recipe! We love cabbage and since it's the day after St. Patrick's day, I had some on hand. After all, soup is about using what you have in your fridge and pantry. I wanted to fill this soup with as much nutrition as possible, so in addition to cabbage, I added a few handfuls of chopped kale, chopped carrot, oregano, thyme (which is excellent for respiratory issues), took the advice of other reviewers and added a dash of cayenne and some red pepper flakes. Since they have great healing properties I increased the onion and garlic. I didn't have any stewed tomatoes, so I used fire roasted diced tomatoes instead. Toward the end of cooking I threw in a small amount of elbow noodles that needed to be used up and for protein, added dark red kidney beans. I cooked it all in low sodium (from Trader Joe's) organic chicken broth and then added some more water and Better Than Bouillon Organic Chicken Base. It tastes amazing and I expect it to be even better tomorrow. Thanks, JGCase, for a great cabbage soup recipe.

This recipe is fantastic!  First of all, to only give it a 4 because "it's not a 5 until you make it your own" is really beyond me...every recipe is made your own in some way more than likely!  I followed everything ingredient wise but used more ingredients than called for.  I used a whole onion (somewhat large yellow onion), equivalent to 4-5 garlic cloves (they were 3 huge ones), the whole head of cabbage, and then of course extra water and added a can of chicken broth since I used extra stuff.  I also chose to use a regular can of stewed tomatoes because I didn't want an Italian spin on the taste.  My husband requested ham to be put in it and so I found Tyson's ham strips (small pieces of ham) and they went perfectly even though it was a chicken based broth.  For the seasoning, I added a little season salt, pepper, and a couple sprinkles of cayenne pepper.  This came out EXCELLENT!  This will more than likely be the soup I make most often.  It is a wonderful recipe, THANK YOU JGCASE!

text:
This is an excellent recipe! It is so flavorful, so easy and so healthy! I took several suggestions from previous reviewers that I will definitely include next time I fix this (which will be soon!). I added 1 tsp of majoram and some chopped baby carrots and celery (had them on hand, didn't want them to go bad). I substituted vegetable broth for chicken bouillon (vegetarian) and seasoned diced tomatoes (basil, garlic, oregano) for the stewed tomatoes. I didn't drain the tomatoes (to retain the seasonings) and the recipe still worked out great. My girlfriend (who usually requires massive amounts of cheese and/or butter to eat vegetables) suggested that I make it every Sunday!  I highly recommend this recipe!

good recipe but since I cant leave well enough alone I modified as follows:

3 cloves garlic
2 medium white onions
2 stalks celery sliced thin to cook with onions/garlic
1 cup of shredded carrots (for additional color)
1 full medium head cabbage
1/4 tsp (or to taste) cayenne pepper
1 quart filtered water
1 quart unsalted chicken broth

My husband and I LOVED this soup!  The only changes I made were to use bone broth and plain organic chopped canned tomatoes, undrained.  The leftovers were even better the next day as the flavors were able to develop more.  I will make it again and have already recommended it to a friend.  Oh, almost forgot....I added two Kielbasa links halved and sliced.  I first browned them before sauteeing the onion.  With the sausage, I did not use the olive oil as there was enough fat, but more added flavor.  Makes me hungry just thinking of how good and satisfying this soup is.  Am making a double batch today for us and dear friends.  Such a good soup that can be customized for your personal preferences if one would like.

Excellent!  One of the best vegetable soups I've tasted!  I also cut up some baby carrots and a stalk of celery, adding some red pepper flakes as others suggested.  I used a whole head of cabbage (a fairly large head) and used canned drained diced tomatoes (since I didn't have stewed Italian style), adding some Italian seasonings for flavor. 2 Tbsp. olive oil;
1 onion, chopped;

48 oz. organic low-sodium chicken broth;

country:
None
text:
Mine is similar, but I got a little creative with the aim for less calories.
1/2 an onion
1/2 medium head of purple cabbage
3 orange/yellow tomatoes (they are lower in acidity)
1 yellow bell pepper
1 green zucchini
4 cups vegetable stock
4 cups water.

Basically, throw the chopped onions in until they look transparent. Cut up all the vegetables into appealing cuts (I like to use different shapes on different vegetables for contrast).  Then throw in the vegetables and let them sweat with the lid on at medium for a bit. then toss in the vegetable stock and water and bring to a boil. this is where you would add your favorite spices if you like, salt (or not), pepper, what ever you want, throw it in. Next, put three servings of your favorite whole wheat noodles in there. once the noodles are soft, bring it down to simmer and let is chill there for an hour (or until all the vegetables are soft). This entire pot contains 1,000 calories.

text:
Very glad I had so much leftover to freeze!  I used 1/2 a head of a cabbage that weighed 4 lbs. I reduced the olive oil to about 1.5 Tbsp, & when the onions were soft, I added in 2 stalks of finely-sliced celery & cooked that with the onion, then added in 4 cloves of minced garlic & cooked a couple minutes longer.  Used chicken-flavored "Better than Bouillon", which comes in a jar.  Added 3 thinly-sliced carrots along with the chopped cabbage. I used the liquid from the tomatoes, also, & ended up cooking an extra 30 minutes (at least).  The flavor really comes together as it cooks, & is even better the next day.

This soup is delicious. I think it really is healing. I feel better right away when I eat it. I make a couple changes to suit my taste. I had two stalks of celery and three carrots, chopped. I cook these with the onion and garlic at the beginning. Also, I either use all chicken stock/broth (the boxed kind), or I use one 32 oz. box of stock, 4 cups of water, and a couple teaspoons of better than boullion. And I buy to canned diced Italian style tomatoes rather than the stewed tomatoes.
When I'm feeling especially lazy, I buy the mirepioux mix from Trader Joes (chopped onions, celery & carrots) and the bagged shredded cabbage. The soup practically cooks itself! And I have a hot cup of soup helping me to feel better in no time. Thanks for a great recipe!

I will be making this one regularly! YUMMY!! I did make some changes, but didn't alter the seasonings and it is really fantastic (even my picky when it comes to new veggies son likes it a lot!) I used 4 cups chicken broth and 4 cups veggie broth instead of bouillon and water. I used a whole small red onion and put that with the 2 garlic cloves in a food processor and got them nice and small. I sauteed that with about 15 baby carrots diced and 2 celery stalks diced. I then followed the rest of the ingredients and instructions as written (I did not drain the tomaotes). At the very end I aso added a can of drained beans for some protein. This was really delicious and feels so good on my stomach. I think I could eat the whole pot! :)

text:
This is a delicious soup for one that's so low in calories.  I tend to like my food salty, but this soup was a little too salty for my liking. I used a whole yellow onion and a whole (small) head of cabbage and the soup came out great. Like others, I also pureed about half of the soup to make it a little smoother and "thicker". Great idea! This soup is an excellent "healing" food, however if you want to make it for dinner rather than recovery, I would suggest adding potatoes and carrots to make it heartier.
warning: dont puree soup (in blender) while HOT...the pressure will make the lid fly off and soup go everywhere.....

text:
I'd give this 4.5 stars, but I don't have the option.  I made this soup with a couple alterations.  I used 2 quarts of organic chicken broth instead of the water and bouillon.  I'm not sure how this would have affected the overall flavor, but I found I needed to add a little more salt that might have been present in the bouillon.    I also had a half bag of frozen carrot slices in the freezer that I threw in, which worked well.  

I made this in my Instant Pot, using the saut√© feature to cook the onions first, then added all other ingredients except the tomatoes and cooked on high pressure for 4 minutes.  I quick-released immediately, and the texture was just right.  I stirred in the tomatoes at the end, and the soup was hot enough to heat them up.

I used canned, already-diced, Italian-style tomatoes and did not drain them; I didn't see the point in wasting the juice.  I know the Italian style tomatoes add the flavor of herbs (particularly basil), but I think when I make this soup again, I'll just go with regular diced tomatoes and try my own seasonings.

country:

text:
I found this to be a great "base" recipe, but I like my soup to have more substance so I added more ingredients. I added 1/2 a kielbasa, diced. I did 3 cloves of garlic (will do 4 next time), added 2 stalks of celery, a full onion, and carrots. I used a mandolin to slice up the celery and carrots. It's super quick and keeps the slices uniform! Instead of going through the hassle of chopping up a cabbage I bought a family size "coleslaw mix" bag (cabbage and carrots) and used that. It's perfect! I put the full can of tomatoes in, juice and all, and added a small can of tomato sauce. I'll also be adding a red or orange bell pepper and zucchini next time. For spices I used 1tsp. pink Himalayan salt, oregano, sweet basil, cayenne pepper, red pepper flakes, Italian seasoning, multi-color ground pepper, a dash of smoked paprika, and a bit of dill. Pepper to taste. Mine came with a kick and I love it. With all the additions it's a 5-star soup, but as is I would have found it very bland.

text:
I made the following modifications based on what I had sitting around at home: (1) I didn't have chicken broth, so I used water plus a can of condensed chicken noodle soup. (2) I used 2/3 of a red onion instead of regular onion. (3) I tripled the garlic, because unlike chicken broth or regular onions, I ALWAYS have lots of garlic at home. (4) I used the full head of cabbage - I had no plans to cook with cabbage the rest of the week, and I don't like to waste food. (5) I used a 28 ounce can of crushed tomatoes. (6) I wound up using a tablespoon of salt instead of a teaspoon, because it just tasted better that way at the end.

The end result was delicious - I think I'd make it the same way again.

text:
I used 64 ounces of chicken stock rather than bullion, garlic powder to taste because I didn't have fresh on hand, and a full onion because I don't like trying to remember to use halfway-used vegetables. 

I also added about a half of a cup of barley  to make for something a bit more filling. It probably could have taken a bit more barley than that, but I was still after a light soup, so I was happy with how it turned out. I was vaguely pulling inspiration from Beaker's Vegetable Barley Soup on this same website, so I also included some chopped carrots and a bay leaf.

I suspect that this soup would have been perfectly tasty without the changes, but it was pretty good with them, too! Very mildly spicy, if you're someone who notices the 'spice' of cabbage and black pepper, with a hint of sweetness too. 

Overall, I'd say that it's a nicely flexible, forgiving recipe. I'm definitely going to keep it around for whenever I'm craving something light and warm.

I took another reviewers idea and added some carrots & celery. It's a good soup--I'm eating a bowl now because my throat's a little sore and it's going down well.

text:
As others have said, I really like this as a base recipe that you can do a lot with.  Super easy and flavorful as is...most ingredients readily on hand.  I followed the recipe exactly, but doubled up the garlic.  I then added some Kimchee that I had on hand to spice it up.  Was REALLY good with this extra kick which should help with clearing a stuffed head.

As an aside...I continue to love this recipe and use it often...especially during cold/flu season.  I tried adding some meat.  I used Roasted Garlic & Gruyere Chees smoked Chicken Sausage from Aidells and it was great.  I simply fried some in the oil prior to adding the onion/garlic.  Don't know if I will do this every time, but it is a viable option if you are looking for some protein.  

I continue to prefer this soup recipe with Kimchee added.  It adds a nice kick to help clear your head and I now wouldn't consider making it without at least a little added.

text:
I've been making this for over 2 years. I found it because I was diagnosed with all kinds of food allergies that were causing me inflammation. This soup has been a godsend. I've altered it in many different ways and each time it's been awesome. I always use chicken broth instead of bullion. I, also, always add celery and use canned crushed tomato. I started with a half of a head of cabbage, but eventually realized that a whole head is perfect for a whole week of meals for 2 people. You can throw all kinds of veggies into this soup. I love it with green beans or bell peppers. Basically, if you have some veggies on their way out, throw them in. I usually eat it with an added protein diced or shredded in it. Every meat works. Sausage or ground turkey have been my fav. The best part is that I always lose weight, during the soup week. I want to thank you for posting this recipe. It's made me feel better when I've been ill and lose weight when I've been fat. What more can you ask for? oh, yea....it tastes good too!

text:
I've made this many times. Usually exactly as listed(which is wonderful!), but I tried a couple of things differently today and it really elevated it. 

Add in one can of Rotel tomatoes with green chilies, and cut up a couple of zucchini into inch chunks. Regular diced canned tomatoes, not the Italian. Lastly I added in a solid pound of chopped carrots. It is amazing.  A dash of lemon juice when you bowl it up and it really kicks it up that little bit. 

I love that this recipe is nothing you need to be exact with. You can adjust it to what you have on hand as well.

One word of caution... the garlic... ahem.. unless everyone's eating the soup.. use cautiously. I'm reasonably certain there's not a vampire around for at least a 10 mile radius.  Ha ha!

text:
I used a full head of cabbage (chopped), 1 1/2 onion, 1 lb of baby carrots, 1 green pepper,  and 12 cups reduced sodium chicken broth and olive oil as needed.   I brought the chicken broth to a boil and put in the chopped cabbage, meanwhile I chopped the onion and pepper and fried in olive oil for about ten minutes.  When cooked I added it in with the cabbage.  No salt, pepper, etc. was added.  After cooking on a low boil for 30-35 minutes I used my immersion mixer to blend the ingredients.  It tastes great and is relatively low in calories.

text:
I have made this simple soup several times and I can't seem to ever get enough!  As a vegetarian, I use part water and part vegetable broth.  I always double it, and find that usually within a week, it's gone.  My boyfriend loves it so much that when he starts to feel poorly, he'll have a steady diet of cabbage soup, ginger tea, and orange juice.  I add fresh carrots (because, hey, who doesn't like carrots?!) and, if I have celery, I chop up some celery and add it, too.  I tend to like a slightly thicker soup, so I'll add croutons but that's me.    I love, Love, LOVE this soup!  I recently saw someone put mushrooms in and I'm definitely going to try that next time this soup is being desired, and in this cold weather, it's desired more and more!

text:
I've never had cabbage soup before, let alone even made it. I don't like Sauerkraut, so I  wasn't interested, but, having half a head of cabbage left over from another beef soup recipe, and having a vegetarian friend over the following day, I decided to look up cabbage soup and stumbled across this one. I made it exactly as specified (except I added celery I also had around), but it seemed to taste a bit bland. Based on reviews, I upped the garlic and chicken broth flavoring (I used "Better than Bouillon" Chicken), upped the salt and pepper a touch, and added some basil and Italian herbs. After simmering, I cautiously tasted the broth. It seemed pretty good. I poured a small bowl. It was really good. I poured another bigger bowl. It was DELICIOUS! I then poured an even bigger bowl full. IT WAS AMAZING! This is among the best soup flavors I've ever experienced. No lie!

text:
This is a really delicious and simple soup to make. I used all organic ingredients including the spices and used 1/2 head Napa / 1/2 head Savoy cabbage. Rather than the bouillon I used some bone marrow broth (I am nearly entirely Paleo) and dried thyme that I grow in my window and keep hanging in my kitchen. I highly recommend adding two pinches of the dried thyme...rally punched it up for me! I also used a fresh carrot sliced thin and 8 cloves of garlic rather than 2. I can literally feel my immunity increasing as I eat it. I will make this again and again...enjoy!

This recipe was very easy to fallow but it needed more umph. I used 2 carrots thinly sliced along with the onion and garlic. text:
An absolutely delicious recipe, and very easy with its limited ingredients.  I was sick and this was so comforting, and my husband raved about how good it was and had the leftovers for breakfast. I did make a few changes based on what I had in the pantry and another cabbage soup recipe I had just seen.  I started by dicing and frying 4 slices of bacon (froze it halfway first to make it easy to dice), drained most of the fat and add 2 tablespoons of olive oil to cook the onion and garlic.  The bacon added a mild richness but did not add a bacon flavor.  Bouillon has way too much salt so I used chicken stock and no added salt. I doubled the tomatoes, and as I didn't have Italian Style Tomatoes used Fire Roasted w/chilies which added just the perfect amount of heat, plus I added 1/2 tsp. of Italian Seasoning.  I served with thick slices of crusty bread!  This will become a regular winter time meal.

Even better than I expected.  I only made a few minor adjustments to the original recipe.  I used 1 whole onion, canned diced tomatoes (undrained), 3 chopped celery stalks, 1/2 beef and 1/2 chicken bouillon, Italian seasoning and dried parsley, omitted the salt, and substituted 2 cups of the water with some thick home-canned, lightly-seasoned tomato juice.  Other than those changes, I followed the recipe, and it turned out to be very flavorful!  The next day I added some leftover ground beef that had been sauteed with Rotel...really good!  Next time I make it, I'll add hamburger to begin with!  Great low-carb recipe!

So good! I tweaked though. I wanted something for my crock pot, so I put in a head of cabbage, approx a box of chicken broth, 2 cans stewed mexican style tomatoes, 2 stalks celery chopped, 1 small onion chopped, 1-2 cups chopped baby carrots, 2 cups sliced mushrooms (sauteed first), 1/4 cup of lentils, and garlic powder. Mix all together in a crock pot and cook on low for 6 hours. I made corn muffins to go with and the sweet with the spicy juices were sooo good! Tasted even better the next day. 
Very good and easily customizable recipe. Perfect for a fall day! :)

Yum!  Like many others, I changed a few things.  I didn't use the 3 Tbsp olive oil, but gave the pot a healthy spray of olive oil spray, instead.  I used a bag of frozen "soup mix" that had a blend of onion, celery, bell pepper, and parsley.  It didn't have much parsley, so I added a little fresh chopped that I had on hand. Excellent and extremely versatile. I used 4tablesp olive oil, 1 onion and 3 cloves garlic. I flavoured the soup with a few sprigs of fresh thyme, 1/2 teasp each dry marjoram and dry rosemary. I used 4 qts water and 2 bouillon cubes. I used 3/4 of a Savoy cabbage. I doubled up on the tomatoes - two 14.5oz cans - and used the liquid from the tomatoes - didn't drain them. I added a large parsnip and 4 carrots both sliced, which sweeten the broth. Delicious. Thanks for the recipe.

This is a good starting point to a great soup, but it lacked flavour for me.  It was also a little too acidic because of the tomatoes.  I will be making it again once I learn more about what seasonings go well with cabbage, and I will be using ready-made chicken broth, because concentrated bouillon didn't seem to add enough taste to the cabbage.  It's still a good soup, and I will eat the rest, but I wouldn't serve it to anyone else, it's just too bland.  As for the amount of oil in this recipe, it could easily be reduced by half.
